## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear dynamics (harmonic oscillations)
**Analysis**: The task describes a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) is the derivative of velocity. The physical relationship likely involves restoring forces depending on position x (linear or nonlinear), damping forces depending on velocity v, and possibly time-dependent external forcing. This falls squarely in the domain of classical mechanics, specifically nonlinear oscillations, encompassing models like the Duffing, van der Pol, and forced oscillators.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x (simple harmonic motion)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping)
- Forced harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (sinusoidal driving)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (dissipative nonlinear oscillator)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear resonator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (self‑excited limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear damping via v³)
- Mixed nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v / (1 + c2 * Abs(v)) (damping with saturation)
- Softening spring cubic: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (positive cubic weakens restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (asymmetric potential, e.g., in some MEMS)
- Pendulum approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (finite‑amplitude simple pendulum)
- Toda oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (exp(-c1 * x) - 1) (exponential nearest‑neighbor potential)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v - c3 * v**3 + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (general forced dissipative nonlinear oscillator)
- Phase‑shifted forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (forced oscillator with phase lag)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force with odd power terms (x, x³) preserves symmetry; an even power term like x² indicates an asymmetric potential.
- Sign of the linear damping term (c * v) distinguishes energy dissipation (dv/dt = … - c*v) from energy injection (… + c*v).
- Cubic x³ term alongside linear x: a positive coefficient (hardening) steepens restoring force; a negative coefficient (softening) flattens it.
- A damping term proportional to (1 – x²)*v characterizes van der Pol oscillators and produces a stable limit cycle (self‑sustained oscillation).
- Presence of a sinusoidal driving term (cos(c*t)) implies forced oscillations; when driving frequency matches natural frequency, resonance occurs.
- Damping proportional to v³ (Rayleigh damping) increases with velocity amplitude, typically modelling high‑speed fluid resistance.
- Exponential restoring force (exp(-x) – 1) appears in Toda lattice and strongly anharmonic solids; it behaves linearly for small x and saturates for large negative x.
- If acceleration depends on sign(x) or sign(v), piecewise forms can model different stiffness for compression vs. extension (bilinear spring).
- Inclusion of a term like 1/(1 + c * v²) in damping models a saturation effect where damping cannot exceed a certain value.
- For large‑amplitude pendulums, dv/dt ∝ –sin(x) introduces a periodic restoring force, leading to amplitude‑dependent frequency.
